  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1298941966" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1298941966" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1298941966?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People Who Wish It Was the 1980s Again</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=published2015">published2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=he-says">he-says</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=american-author">american-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1298941966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16205192272001966273"><i>I tried to keep my cool. I tried to remain skeptical. I reminded myself that I was a man of science, even if I did usually get a C in it.<br/><br/>I looked at it again. I still couldn't tell what it was, but I knew what it wasn't - it wasn't a meteor. Or a weather balloon, or swamp gas, or ball lightning. No, the unidentified flying object I was staring at with my own two eyes was most definitely NOT OF THIS EARTH.<br/><br/>My first thought was: Holy fucking shit.</i><br/><br/>How much jerking-off to '80s nostalgia can one man d</span>
  <span id="freeText16205192272001966273" style="display:none"><i>I tried to keep my cool. I tried to remain skeptical. I reminded myself that I was a man of science, even if I did usually get a C in it.<br /><br />I looked at it again. I still couldn't tell what it was, but I knew what it wasn't - it wasn't a meteor. Or a weather balloon, or swamp gas, or ball lightning. No, the unidentified flying object I was staring at with my own two eyes was most definitely NOT OF THIS EARTH.<br /><br />My first thought was: Holy fucking shit.</i><br /><br />How much jerking-off to '80s nostalgia can one man do? Ernest Cline is testing my limits as he's written not one but TWO full-length novels crammed to the gills with '80s references.<br /><br />Listen, I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One" title="Ready Player One by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a> and liked it. A lot of people did. Unfortunately, Cline has interpreted us liking that book as a green-light to write more books that center around the worship of everything '80s.<br /><br />Seems as if Cline is a one-trick pony.<br /><br />Stop me if you've heard this one. Zack Lightman is good at basically nothing except playing video games. Specifically one video game that deals with fighting off an alien invasion. One day, Men in Black come to his school and recruit him to fight aliens for real - the video game was actually a recruiting tool for the upcoming war against aliens from Europa. Sound familiar?<br /><br />Yeah.<br /><br />ANYWAY, I would be absolutely fine with this tired-ass plot if Cline bothered to add anything new or interesting to it. But he doesn't.<br /><br />Worse than that, Zack and all the other characters in this book do not emote. Instead of having feelings, they simply compare themselves to fictional '80s characters. For instance, when Zack sees a space shuttle land near his school - one that is ripped right from the video game he plays incessantly - he doesn't talk about how he feels. Instead, he<br /><br /><i>Okay, then you might be trapped inside a lucid dream, like Tom Cruise in Vanilla Sky. Or maybe your reality is really just an incredibly convincing computer simulation, like in The Matrix. Or maybe you just died in a car accident, and this is all just an elaborate fantasy playing out in your brain during the last few seconds of your life - like in that one old Twilight Zone episode.</i><br /><br />The characters do not have feelings that belong to themselves, only to other pop-culture fictional characters.<br /><br />What about when he sees the advanced army base full of anti-alien craft? How does he feel?<br /><br /><i>In that moment, I felt like Luke Skywalker surveying a hangar full of A-, Y-, and X-Wing Fighters just before the Battle of Yavin. Or Captain Apollo, climbing into the cockpit of his Viper on the Galactica's flight deck. Ender Wiggin arriving at Battle School. Or Alex Rogan, clutching his Star League uniform, staring wide-eyed at a hangar full of Gunstars.<br /><br />But this wasn't a fantasy. I wasn't Buck Rogers or Flash Gordon or Ender Wiggin or anyone else. This was real life. My life.</i><br /><br /><br />And Cline never puts just ONE '80s reference into an explanation when he can fit in three. It's highly annoying. Also, he is going to spoil innumerable movies and tv shows for you. You have been warned. Read at your own risk.<br /><br />Let's look at a scene where a school bully has scratched Zack's car.<br /><br /><i>One of the few perks of driving an ancient, rusted-out shit wagon was that it took real effort to make it look any less aesthetically pleasing than it already was.<br /><br />This realization allowed me to calm myself enough to heed the whispered advice of Master Yoda now on repeat in my head: Let go of your anger.<br /><br />I often tried to calm myself with Yoda's voice (which sounded nothing like Fozzie Bear, damn you) during moments of distress. Obi-Wan or Qui-Gon or Mace Windu sometimes had calming movie-quote wisdom to share to.<br /><br />That was only on good days, of course. On the bad ones, I found myself drawing on equally compelling advice from Lords Vader or Palpatine.</i><br /><br />Please brace yourself for about 5 to 20 pop-culture '80s references on each and every page.<br /><br /><br />Who really cares enough about the 1980s to read and beat-off to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One" title="Ready Player One by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a> AND then is immediately hungry for more non-stop 1980s porn?<br /><br />Really, honestly, I am asking. Who is the audience for this book?<br /><br />I know the '80s. I like the '80s. I'm not a real gamer, so most of Cline's video game worship goes right over my head, but I get 95% of his movie references in here and most of his musical ones, too.<br /><br />But what exactly is the point? There's no real plot, and what little plot there is is SO cliched and SO predictable that it's almost not worth reading. I know people like nostalgia, but WHO is reading this?<br /><br />Do teenagers nowadays love, worship and know 1980s culture? NO. At most they have a bit of passing interest in it.<br /><br />Most adults I know, even if they were in their kid or teen years during the '80s, have a limited tolerance for '80s reminiscing if they even care to reminisce at all.<br /><br />I'm highly worried about Cline. Is he stuck in the '80s? I would agree that the 1980s was a heyday for good movie making. However, - and I know this might be a huge shock to Cline - but good movies and tv shows are being made TODAY. *gasp* Yes, I know, it's true. Perhaps he should venture out to an actual theater or turn on his tv to HBO or Showtime instead of re-watching Back to the Future for the fiftieth time. The author picture of him is him posing with his DeLorean. Now, sweet. I love DeLoreans. Obviously. I loved the BTTF trilogy, SO MUCH. I have parts of it memorized. <br /><br />However, I do NOT wish the '80s would come back, nor do I live in the past. I enjoy consuming modern pop culture and do not believe everything created after 1989 is trash. I'm always weirded out by people who are obsessed with the past and determined to live in it. I'd rather have a new movie with new ideas than a remake of TOTALL RECALL or TRON or yet another TERMINATOR movie. I do not know if Cline has kids, but perhaps if he does they can introduce their dad to some new and cool stuff. He can show them Die Hard and Predator and they can show him something that was made after 2005. It will blow his mind.<br /><br /><br />We also have some HIGHLY annoying "plot points" in the book which I will cover now.<br /><br />1.) Absolute dream girl. Zack, on the first day - no, first HOUR - of training meets a black-clad, tattooed, older (he's 18, she's 22) woman who thinks he's cute and actually lets him sit by her instead of telling him to fuck off. She instantly gets all of his '80s jokes and references and ALSO is apparently obsessed with the '80s, so... they should get married immediately or something. I'm not even saying insta-love, I'm saying 'mythical dream girl that automatically likes you and appears immediately on your first day. You will have to do nothing to impress her, everything that comes out of your mouth is gold.'<br /><br />This annoyed me to no end. She has no personality - much like Zack - and just exists to be his badass perfect girlfriend, a relationship that happens instantly, with none of that pesky getting-to-know-you, dating, can-I-trust-you, falling-in-love stuff that one normally has to go through in order to have a relationship.<br /><br />2.) There's one gay couple in the novel and they <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[die. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Yeah. It's 2015 and we're still dealing with this shit.<br /><br />3.) This is what annoyed me the most:<br /><br /><i>I nodded, still trying to rein in my conflicting emotions. Everything I'd ever been told or taught about the state of the world had been a lie. I 'd grown up believing that despite our aspirations, humans were still just a bunch of bipedal apes, divided into arbitrary tribes that were constantly at war over their ruined planet's dwindling natural resources. I'd always assumed that our future would end up looking more like Mad Max than Star Trek. But now I was forced to see our rampant fossil fuel consumption - and our seeming disregard for its effect on our already-changing climate - in an entirely new light. We hadn't used up all our of oil and ravaged our planet in a mindless pursuit of consumerism, but in preparation for a dark day most of us hadn't even known was coming.<br /><br />Even humanity's lack of concern for its rampant overpopulation problem now made a terrible kind of sense. What difference did it make if our planet was capable of supporting all seven billion of us in the long term when a far greater threat to our numbers was waiting in the wings? And despite the overwhelming odds, humanity had done what was necessary to ensure its own survival. It filled me with a strange new sense of pride in my own species. We weren't a primitive bunch of monkeys teetering on the brink of self-destruction after all - this appeared to be an altogether different kind of destruction we were teetering on the brink of.</i><br /><br />Fuck you.<br /><br />Seriously, this made me angrier and more annoyed than anything else in the entire book. I was livid.<br /><br />40 pages later, this reiterates when<br /><br /><i>"You're looking at the real reason for the recent global financial crisis - all of human civilization's technology, industry, and natural resources have been leveraged to the hilt in our effort to ensure that we have the firepower necessary to repel the invaders' superior numbers and advanced weaponry. And now, at long last, our forces are ready for deployment."</i><br /><br />Fuck you, fuck you! I was getting very upset.<br /><br />4.) This book is a lot like watching someone else play a video game.<br /><br /><b>What are you saying?</b><br /><br />I'm saying the book is fucking boring, is what I'm saying. The fights and combat is video game fighting and combat. And you are certainly not in control. All the battle scenes and fighting is boring as hell.<br /><br /><br />Also, is Cline ever going to craft a MC who is NOT a Gary-Stu teenaged boy? How long can this go on? I feel like he's got a bit of Salinger in him. Branch out! Don't be scared. <br /><br /><br />Tl;dr - This is just another rehash of Cline's basic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One" title="Ready Player One by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a> plot. <br /><br />'80s worship, knowledge, and pop culture is life! But EVEN MORE SO than in RP1! Playing video games non-stop as a teen is actually a very valuable use of your time that will pay off big time! BUT EVEN MORE SO than in RP1! Our hero is a Gary Stu! BUT EVEN MORE SO than in RP1! <br /><br />Do you think that you need even MORE masturbatory material about how FUCKING AMAZING the 1980s were!?!!? I mean, no other decade even compares to the 1980s! Do you just watch 1980s specials on VH1 for hours and hours on end? Only listen to 1980s music? Only play video games on (original) Nintendo and Atari? Only watch movies that were made in this awesome decade!?!? Why bother living in the present?<br /><br />If so, Armada is the book for you! You can read it and laugh at all the '80s jokes. You can lovingly remember all your favorite '80s games, movies, tv shows, and video games! I mean, sure the book was published in 2015, but we can forgive it for that, certainly?!!?<br /><br />However, if you seek new material in your books: fresh plots, actual character development, and things that are relevant in this decade, perhaps you would like to read something else. I'm still trying to figure out who Cline's audience is. One shot of '80s nostalgia was fun. Two shots is making me sick to my stomach. This fell very flat to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16205192272001966273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1355488186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1355488186" />
    <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey"><img alt="Mohammed Arabey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364338486p2/13592557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1355488186?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mohammed Arabey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mohammed Arabey" href="/user/show/13592557-mohammed-arabey">Mohammed Arabey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1355488186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12021566096737788405">So,<b> July, 14 2015</b> couldn't be any more accurate release date for <b>"ARMADA"</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439650895i/15866650._SX540_.jpg' width='450' height='252' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I mean,<br/><b>March, 24 2015<br/>The X-Files</b> 'Worldwide Popular 90s TV Series Started 1993' returns in new 6 episodes next year, after 13 years since it ended.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454805203i/18016397._SX540_.jpg' width='450' height='267' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>April, 20 2015<br/>Independence Day: Resurgence</b>, sequel to major 1996 international blockbuster, began filming 20 years since the first one.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439651259i/15866719._SX540_.jpg' width='450' height='192' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>& to Sci-Facts..</i><br/><b>July, 14 2015<br/>Pluto</b>, the planet..finally got close-up images & detailed observations of it and its moons.<blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439650895i/15866652.jpg' width='297' height='479' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><b>July, 23 2015<br/>Earth 2.</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12021566096737788405" style="display:none">So,<b> July, 14 2015</b> couldn't be any more accurate release date for <b>"ARMADA"</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439650895i/15866650._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="252" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I mean,<br><b>March, 24 2015<br>The X-Files</b> 'Worldwide Popular 90s TV Series Started 1993' returns in new 6 episodes next year, after 13 years since it ended.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454805203i/18016397._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="267" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>April, 20 2015<br>Independence Day: Resurgence</b>, sequel to major 1996 international blockbuster, began filming 20 years since the first one.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439651259i/15866719._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="192" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>&amp; to Sci-Facts..</i><br><b>July, 14 2015<br>Pluto</b>, the planet..finally got close-up images &amp; detailed observations of it and its moons.<blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439650895i/15866652.jpg" width="297" height="479" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><b>July, 23 2015<br>Earth 2.0 </b>announced by NASA. Kepler-452b, A planet discovered very similar to Earth and potentially habitable.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439651121i/15866702.jpg" width="450" height="327" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b><br>And with a very clever plot, with decent and some mind blowing twists, here comes Armada.. Mixing other Sci-Fiction Novels, Movies and Video Games and their releasing dates with Sci-Facts and a HUGE conspiracy theory..<br></b><br>First I have to admit that's I'm not a fan of Star Wars, Star Trek, Ender's Game ,even Battleship and all space fight kind of crap <i>"Ooops sorry fans"</i>.. I'm not even a good devoted gamer..<br> But still I'm a geek kinda way..<br> I mean I'm a huge fan of<b> The X-Files</b> and the Conspiracy Theories about Aliens. And I'm okay with Independence Day's main plot without much of crap video games fights.. just what serve the plot.<br><b><br>I want to Believe, but I'm not willing to live in a video game worlds and unrealistic space and UFO fight crab... Just Want to Believe....<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439651660i/15866816._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="189" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> ***** <u>The Story </u> begans with Zack Lightman, a high school student, spotting a flying saucer while staring out his classroom window..<br></b><i><br>'What's the hell...it started just like that? Is he sure he wasn't just starting at a poster in Fox Mulder's office?<br>Okay, first chapter and I'm outta here. And won't rate it, it wouldn't be fair. Future with Aliens goofing around is NOT my type of read.. </i><br>Back to Chapter 1<br><b><br>Then,we see that Zack has a pretty good backstory, he's likeable and interesting character to read...<br>And, most importantly, Turns out spotting a flying saucer is unusal and kinda crazy in the world of the story</b>.<br>That is good for me..So why not reading another chapter?<br><br> <b> Zack thinking he gone mad like his geeky father who passed away at the age 19, Zack may never remember him alive, he died when Zack was less than a year old.. <br><br>He goes into his father old possessions and re-read a note that made him disturbed before..<br>it seems that his father was connecting since the 70s till his passing away in 1999 every sci-fi blockbuster movies,Aliens invasion novels and space wars games releasing dates, and connecting it with interesting conspiracy theories about it. Specially with a very good use of an urban legend about video gaming machines. <br><blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439671610i/15870409._SY540_.png" width="300" height="330" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote>
<br>His father thought that the Military or NASA preparing people by these movies and novels for the news that we are not alone in the universe.. and we may have Alien Invasion....soon!!!!!<br>AND all the games and tracking the top players is to train a new army of Gamers..to be real Soliders..<br></b><br><i> And that's what I did at the beginning of the review...connecting the dots just like Zack's Father notes.. oh and here's more..<br><br><b>April 16, 2015<br>Star Wars </b>is baaaaack, 2nd Trailer for the third trilogy that will hit cinemas next December after 10 years since the end of the second trilogy.<br><b>April 20, 2015<br>Star Wars Anthology</b> for next year release in another side story of Star Wars Universe...<br><br>And don't forget <b>Gravity </b>2013, <b>Interstellar</b> 2014 ..the Oscar's sweethearts who will get a new bro, <b>The Martian </b>2015... <br>YEAH I'm getting paranoid just like Zack's father...Thank you very much Ernest Cline.<br></i><b><br>So , to get raid of these crazy thoughts that he saw a flying saucer, he decided to stop gaming for few days.. <br>He plays Armada.. a worldwide Earth Vs. Aliens online multiplayer game.. <br>but he just must do one big mission to keep his top 10 rank before his short quitting...a mission to destroy the Alien planet..the EDA 'Earth Defense Alliance' depends on them.<br><br>Long story short, the mission failed ... and Zack finds out the day after that his father was right...they are not controlling Drones in Armada Game...they controlling it in real life War....Organized by EDA...which now really depends on the real gamers....all around the world. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439672610i/15870571._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>*****************<br>That was the first few chapters 'Phase One' of thks amazingly written novel..<br><br>And man , oh man.. I'm not space gamer at all and get bored of watching one in the Star Wars movies , sorry fans again, BUT the way Ernest wrote it in phase one was more than interesting and get me hooked with the story..<br>It is way better with more convincing plot by using remote Drones , like controlling space ships and Big robots by your home PC, taplets, or gaming devices. <br><br>And what I loved more the deeper message and moral of the story..<br><br><u> Humanity and Wars</u><br>I love how the novel profiling how wars begins...how it's always stars with minor or stupid misunderstanding...<br></b><i>
  <blockquote>All war is deception.<br>If we don't end war, war will end us</blockquote>
</i><b><br>With perfect mix of lovable characters, nostalgic memories full of songs, movies and novels you find that you're really fighting with them for humanity... no matter how the fight gets bigger and bigger...you're in..<br>Even if you're, like me , not a gamer at all, you'll love to read it..and play.<br>♡♡♡♡♡♡♡♡♡♡♡<br>Plot twists, and I loved using mature characters, since I'm sick of YA with all the main characters are 14 to 16. The rest are useless.<br><br>Having a religious positive character, and making clear that religion is not far from our real world was beyond awesome, since I feel sick that all characters in other novels just don't believe in God or anything. <br>There was an unnecessary gay relation but that's okay.<br><br>By the end...I was so teary and emotionally touched ...I loved it so much, I loved all the twists and characters...<br>I doubt if I need a part 2...But this one was really perfect with awesome ending..I Loved it..<br><br>And now , I'm already feeling nostalgic to the Armada game..EDA..The Moon Base..and Mr.Lightman's mix tape. <br><blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439674376i/15870774.jpg" width="345" height="345" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></blockquote>
<br></b> <i>The latter reminds me much with Chris Pratt in Guardians of the Galaxy..but that's okay, I liked him too.</i><b> <br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>ACKNOWLEDGEMENT<br></b><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439674376i/15870775._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="272" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> I'd never bought this novel if I've read the plot..or even the first couple of lines 'the flying saucer :)'.I'd thought it'd be teenager vs aliens kind of game..<br>I just bought it cause it released first time in Egypt at the same international release day, which happens to be my birthday <i> 'BTW thank you Cherry Blossom Books'</i> <br>Also there's excellent praise for the author's debut novel..how geeky and nostalgic he is 'which apply to me as well kinda way'...<br>And I now so glad that I got it.. Ernest is really talented geeky author and successfully got me into his game..<br><b> I am not a gamer and not Sci-Fi big fan...But Armada become one of my very favourite read this year, and may be all time too..<br></b><br>Many pitching around 'Ready Player One' was better, but why comparing? I didn't read it yet but now I'm more than exciting to read it too.<br><br>Till we play again in Ready Player One..<br><br>Mohammed Arabey<br>Playing<br>from 5 August 2015<br>to 9 August 2015</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1398010975" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1398010975?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1398010975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16638914950972249770">A stoned gamer’s fantasy.<br/><br/>Ernest Cline, you had me at “pass the blue milk, Aunt Beru”.<br/><br/>Author Ernest Cline follows up his brilliant 2011 novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One' title='Ready Player One by Ernest Cline' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ready Player One</a> with 2015’s Armada. Not as epic or as good (in any way) as its predecessor Armada does feature Cline’s inimitable ability to weave elements of pop culture, especially gaming and SF/F, into a fun adventure.<br/><br/>At best it is a cool Pink Floyd song, at worst a stupid Adam Sandler film. Armada tells the story of Zack Lightman, a gamer hero who has </span>
  <span id="freeText16638914950972249770" style="display:none">A stoned gamer’s fantasy.<br><br>Ernest Cline, you had me at “pass the blue milk, Aunt Beru”.<br><br>Author Ernest Cline follows up his brilliant 2011 novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One" title="Ready Player One by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a> with 2015’s Armada. Not as epic or as good (in any way) as its predecessor Armada does feature Cline’s inimitable ability to weave elements of pop culture, especially gaming and SF/F, into a fun adventure.<br><br>At best it is a cool Pink Floyd song, at worst a stupid Adam Sandler film. Armada tells the story of Zack Lightman, a gamer hero who has lost his father and his way amidst an uncaring universe. But wait! All’s not what it seems, and Cline packs a full picnic of tasty similes, munchilicious metaphors and a fun sized cornucopia of pop culture references into a passable gamerpunk Frank Capra feelgooder. <br><br>Ready Player One was a fun ride of 80s trivia, but it also had a solid story and a conflict that held the reader’s attention. Armada is told with Cline’s wit and erudite understating of all things SF, served up with a heaping side order of quotes and citations to film, song and graphic novel, but much of the storyline feels contrived. Borrowing heavily from such classics as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375802.Ender_s_Game__Ender_s_Saga___1_" title="Ender's Game (Ender's Saga, #1) by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Ender's Game</a>, Last Starfighter and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4982.The_Sirens_of_Titan" title="The Sirens of Titan by Kurt Vonnegut" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sirens of Titan</a> Cline mails in a follow-up in lieu of a straight up sequel.<br><br>In the winter of 1986 I went to the movies with some friends to see the action film Iron Eagle. What is very memorable to me about this very forgettable lame ass flick was the realization that I would one day criticize and review popular media. We left the cinema and I was shocked to hear that my friends liked the swill. “What the hell? That was several latitudes south of stupid. A rock and roller 18 year old kid who steals an F-18 to rescue his dad? Really? I wasted $3.35 minimum wage coinage that I could have better used towards underage consumption???” I find it no small coincidence that Cline references Iron Eagle shamelessly.<br><br>Not bad.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467507547i/19600313.jpg" width="280" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16638914950972249770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_702120923" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/702120923" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/702120923?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer702120923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6826228826457476922">This book gave me an epiphany and that's not always a good thing apparently.<br/><br/>Up to the moment I read this book, I'd started to convince myself that really the main thing that mattered to me in a book was readability. How much was a both looking forward to reading a book and how fast were the pages turning for me? Those are two things I thought a great deal of in terms of esteem (and star rating points).<br/><br/>Armada had all that. I did look forward to reading it and I thought the pages turned rather qui</span>
  <span id="freeText6826228826457476922" style="display:none">This book gave me an epiphany and that's not always a good thing apparently.<br /><br />Up to the moment I read this book, I'd started to convince myself that really the main thing that mattered to me in a book was readability. How much was a both looking forward to reading a book and how fast were the pages turning for me? Those are two things I thought a great deal of in terms of esteem (and star rating points).<br /><br />Armada had all that. I did look forward to reading it and I thought the pages turned rather quickly all in all. <br /><br />But I started to realize that even though I was enjoying myself, I didn't really think all that much of this story. It's rather bland for the most part and so chalk full of 80's nerdery it's almost as if no other nerdery is allowed or considered worthy.<br /><br />Now, this 80's geekiness works really well in Cline's debut, Ready Player One (How do I love thee? Let me count the ways...), because it's essential to the story. Maybe we should add, because it was new, but I don't know if you can go that far. When the premise revolves around the 80s it just works.<br /><br />Here, Armada's 80's affiliation has more to do with a kid's dead father's obsession and begins to grate in all the wrong ways. It's as if this geeky kid never realized there were other nerdy things to do ... even though he's obsessed with a very hyper-futuristic video game that all kids his age are obsessed with. It'd've been fine with additional, modern references - 80's references are fine - it's just that it begins to sound like that's the only worthy decade when that's far from the truth and arguably only the beginning of a very many great decades for geekery that only got better.<br /><br />It's reinforced by the fact that only those other characters who also know 80's lore are considered with it, cool, on fleek (that's what the kids are saying these days right? *cough* *cough*).<br /><br />To reiterate it's like the emphasis makes it seem like you're only cool (geeky) if you're up on your 80's geekery. If not, you're not actually a geek.<br /><br />Now, I don't want to act like I didn't like Armada. I enjoyed it quite a bit and I admit that my expectations were nigh-on insurmountable after how much I fell for Ready Player One. I still enjoyed Armada, I just won't be fondly remembering my time with the book like I still do with RPO. It's a fun romp and I've forgone mention of the inconsistencies I saw (I think I gave it a hard enough time as is). <br /><br />I'll still be scooping up Cline's next book, but probably not with as much fervor. Expectations have been tempered.<br /><br />3 out of 5 Stars (recommended with reservations)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6826228826457476922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_965886740" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/965886740" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/965886740?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer965886740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1105341276217453837"><i>
  <b>"Kill or be killed. Conquer or be conquered. Survive or go extinct."</b>
</i><br/><br/>My review of Cline's first novel: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/961177190?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ready Player One</a><br/><br/>If you clicked on the link above and read my review of RPO, you would know that I was completely blown away by his first novel. RPO will always be my favorite novel of all time, and that fact managed to alter my expectations when it comes to the Sci-Fi genre. I haven't read a novel as good as RPO, but hopefully I'd find one soon. After I finished it last year, I checked if Cl</span>
  <span id="freeText1105341276217453837" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"Kill or be killed. Conquer or be conquered. Survive or go extinct."</b>
</i><br /><br />My review of Cline's first novel: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/961177190?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a><br /><br />If you clicked on the link above and read my review of RPO, you would know that I was completely blown away by his first novel. RPO will always be my favorite novel of all time, and that fact managed to alter my expectations when it comes to the Sci-Fi genre. I haven't read a novel as good as RPO, but hopefully I'd find one soon. After I finished it last year, I checked if Cline had other novels published, and unfortunately none were in existence. Armada was more than a year away, and I was honestly expecting this to be just as good, if not better. If you would ask me what my first reaction was while reading the novel, I'd say I was disappointed halfway through. In the end though, I had mixed emotions. Mixture of sadness, happiness, disappointment, and an inexpressible feeling of wanting for more. <br /><br />I will not compare RPO and Armada in this review. Yes, I liked the former more than the latter, but Armada was good in its own way. It deserves a proper review. If you're looking for someone who did a comparison of the two, then I'd suggest reading someone else's review. The first paragraph was more of a backstory of why I read this novel in the first place, and the shorter version of the reason would be that Ernest Cline is one of my favorite authors ever, and also because the premise of Armada was compelling as fuck.<br /><br />Let's talk about the plot. I heard a copious amount of comparison between Armada and The Last Starfighter. Even the author himself mentioned TLS in the novel itself, and I will honestly say that I haven't seen TLS. I had no idea what the plot was, so I read Armada and thought that the idea was fairly original. I've heard of the whole thing before, of course, but I haven't had much experience with it before. I'm sure I've watched something similar, but nothing recently so I didn't have much to compared it with. This could be the reason why i enjoyed this more as compared to most disappointed readers. <br /><br />What I didn't like about the plot would be the very dragging first 1/3 of the novel. I hated how Cline introduced everything. At first I didn't even like the characters at all, and the plot was boring for me. If I didn't know much of the author beforehand, I would've DNF this. It was that bad, but then the middle part happened. The action started to happen, and the development finally kicked in. The characters were more witty and funny, and I believe that helped a lot. I had a clue on what the ending would be, and once again sadly I was right. No plot twist whatsoever <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Aside from his dad dying <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and I hate it when that happens. <br /><br />Like I just said, the characters started to develop better in the middle portion, and I learned to like most of them. Zack can be considered your typical main character when it comes to Sci-Fi novels, but I still liked him a lot. His decisions in the novel were a bit out of the ordinary. I like a character who deviates from sanity, but with the right amount of insanity. I can't talk much of the other character without spoiling, so let's just say there might be some plot twists for you guys. You might not see it coming, unlike me.<br /><br />The ending was great for me. I know a lot of people complained about it, but fortunately it was good for me. I liked how he ended things, even though it was a bit cliche. I only really wish for something specific to happen in the end if I liked the characters, and it's a great thing that I was attached to most of them.<br /><br />I played a lot of geeky stuff growing up, so plus points for Cline, once again. I like to read about the games I used to play before. It gives me good feeling of how great my childhood was, and that other people experienced some of the retro goodness that i did. it didn't have much geek stuff incorporated, but I guess it's fine because the author managed to make to plot better in the end.<br /><br />Mostly books tend to lose a star because of the ending, but fortunately it was the other way around for Armada. I was sure about giving this 3 stars, but then the last 1/3 of the novel happened, then I decided to give it another important star. Most people would consider 3 stars as an indication that the novel was bad, but for me most of my 3 star ratings meant that I still enjoyed the novel. I guess I won't have to confuse people now with this 4 star review.<br /><br />3.5/5 stars. I decided to round it up because the novel was great as a whole. If you want a great geeky Sci-Fi novel, then don't hesitate to pick this up. I'd also like to add in that you should buy the hardcover edition of this, because the design is spectacular! Not just the book itself, but also the dust jacket. You'll understand what I'm talking about if you manage to get a copy yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1105341276217453837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5337343132622894071">1.5/5 stars<br/>This book felt like an endless struggle. <br/>At no point did I feel connected to the characters or their plight. The story lacked originality and felt like a mashup of Red Dawn, ET and Close Encounters that is sold as a new inventive plot.<br/><br/>The constant pop culture references became extremely tiring and forced. Often they did not make sense in the context of the story and characters: it's funny how every single character regardless of age immediately gets obscure references to the 80's and </span>
  <span id="freeText5337343132622894071" style="display:none">1.5/5 stars<br />This book felt like an endless struggle. <br />At no point did I feel connected to the characters or their plight. The story lacked originality and felt like a mashup of Red Dawn, ET and Close Encounters that is sold as a new inventive plot.<br /><br />The constant pop culture references became extremely tiring and forced. Often they did not make sense in the context of the story and characters: it's funny how every single character regardless of age immediately gets obscure references to the 80's and 90's.<br /><br />Overall I felt extremely disappointed with this book. I expected something new and original and instead felt like it was a re-write of Ready Player one only with less complex characters and story arc. The characters felt unrealistic and one dimensional and the writing itself lacked depth.<br /><br />I wouldn't mind reading another book by Cline, but I do hope that his next work tackles some new and original material. </span>

<div id="review_783269737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/783269737" />
    <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc"><img alt="Mogsy (MMOGC)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286325553p2/4379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/783269737?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mogsy (MMOGC)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mogsy (MMOGC)" href="/user/show/4379514-mogsy-mmogc">Mogsy (MMOGC)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=arcs-and-galleys">arcs-and-galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=review-copy">review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=gaming">gaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4379514-mogsy-mmogc?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer783269737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2820293272496250516">4 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bibliosanctum.com/2015/07/14/book-review-armada-by-ernest-cline/'>http://bibliosanctum.com/2015/07/14/b...</a><br/><br/>For fans of Ernest Cline’s Ready Player One, I don’t think there’s any other book coming out this year as highly anticipated as his second novel Armada. The new book is again a novel with pop culture references galore, but whereas Ready Player One was like a love letter to the 80s set in not-too-distant future, Armada takes place in present day with a shift in focus to all things sci-fi and gaming.<br/><br/>Needless to say, as an a</span>
  <span id="freeText2820293272496250516" style="display:none">4 of 5 stars at The BiblioSanctum: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bibliosanctum.com/2015/07/14/book-review-armada-by-ernest-cline/">http://bibliosanctum.com/2015/07/14/b...</a><br /><br />For fans of Ernest Cline’s Ready Player One, I don’t think there’s any other book coming out this year as highly anticipated as his second novel Armada. The new book is again a novel with pop culture references galore, but whereas Ready Player One was like a love letter to the 80s set in not-too-distant future, Armada takes place in present day with a shift in focus to all things sci-fi and gaming.<br /><br />Needless to say, as an avid gamer with particular penchant towards massively multiplayer online (MMO) games, I must shamelessly confess to having a natural inclination to stories of this type; more than once, reading Armada made me wish that Eve Online and Dust 514 played like the games described in the book, or that Star Citizen was released already. And I think if you enjoyed Ready Player One, you might enjoy this one too. In many ways the two books are different, but in many ways they are similar as well — both are stories about average young men in the position to save the world, thanks to their super awesome Powers of the Geek!<br /><br />We begin the story with an introduction to our protagonist Zack Lightman, worrying that he might be losing his mind. Staring outside the window during one his boring senior math classes, Zack spies a flying saucer in the sky, and not just any kind of flying saucer. The spaceship looks exactly like an enemy Glaive fighter in Armada, his favorite first-person space combat flight sim MMO. In the game, players from all over take the role of drone pilots, controlling Earth Defense Alliance ships to do battle with alien invaders. Zack’s been playing the game so much, he’s starting to think he’s hallucinating it in his real life as well.<br /><br />Turns out, the good news is that Zack’s not crazy. The enemy fighter he glimpsed was as real as it could be. The bad news is, so is the Earth Defense Alliance and the war against the aliens. Governments around the world have known about this imminent attack for decades, and all the science fiction films and video games since the 70s have been preparing humanity for this very moment. Since their inception, online games like Armada and its companion ground-based first-person shooter Terra Firma have been training and honing the skills of potential recruits for the coming battle, right under everyone’s noses. As one of the highest ranked players in Armada, Zack is enlisted with other skilled gamers into the EDA’s forces.<br /><br />It should have been a dream come true. In fact, the entire book reads like a wish fulfillment fantasy for any gamer who has ever wanted their favorite video game to be real, and to be the big damn hero of their own epic adventure. But still, Zack can’t shake the feeling that there’s something wrong. For example, if this real, why then are the aliens acting exactly like the way they would in his games and in all the science-fiction movies he grew up with? Zach realizes that life is imitating art when it really shouldn’t be – and it’s this concept that erodes the idea that Armada is just another version of The Last Starfighter but Ernest Cline style. Yes, the author has adapted that theme for his book, but at the same time he’s also subverted it, so that certain sections almost read like a tongue-in-cheek, satirical look at what audiences today expect to see out of an alien invasion story.<br /><br />The story of Armada is thus actually quite clever, despite it being undeniably cheesy. We reach a saturation point with many of its ideas – some of which border on the totally ridiculous – that frequently call for a good deal of suspension of disbelief on the reader’s part (and not least because entrusting the fate of the entire human race to a bunch of regular civilian gamers is a dubious idea; if you even spend three minutes exposed to the general chat of any popular MMO, you can kind of infer why). And yet, the book is also undeniably fun. Simply put, the cheese works. It worked the same way it worked for a film like Galaxy Quest which parodied a lot of well-known Star Trek and sci-fi tropes, but somehow in the end still managed to function incredibly well as its own action-adventure stand alone. The result is that it’s still possible for someone not familiar with gamer culture or references to sci-fi movies like Star Wars (of which there are many) to enjoy Armada. However, writing as an addict to online gaming and all things Star Wars, I think that in many ways Armada can also be seen as lovely tribute to fans.<br /><br />It does seem, though, that Ernest Cline has chosen his target audience and defined his niche, pressing the same hot buttons that brought him success with Ready Player One. He employs similar gimmicks in Armada, appealing to the reader’s sense of nostalgia while loading the book with lots of movie quotes and injecting a similar style of humor. A lot would depend on the individual reader, of course, but whether audiences will embrace this shtick again or demand something different, I think only time will tell. We’re also focusing less on general 80s this time around, so I think the appeal will also be much narrower, and it’s possible that those who really liked Ready Player One might not find the same enjoyment in Armada.<br /><br />All told, my own stance is simple: if you’re just looking for a fun read, you’ll get it in spades. While the plot and characters in Armada aren’t particularly deep, the book certainly isn’t aiming to be a literary masterpiece. Instead, it goes for broke, not caring how far it goes in its quest to provide the maximum entertainment value for your time. As a result, Armada ends up being pure, unadulterated escapism. I loved the book, devouring it as soon as I got my hands on it and I sure don’t regret doing so at all. I can think of no other science fiction novel coming out this summer that would make a better beach read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2820293272496250516" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1317857718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1317857718" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1317857718?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1317857718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4517813423222992812"><i>"I was staring out the classroom window and daydreaming of adventure when I spotted the flying saucer."</i><br/><br/>From the very first sentence of the book, Ernest Cline takes the reader on a heart-pounding, laser-shooting, smile-inducing adventure. Fans of his first novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One' title='Ready Player One by Ernest Cline' rel='nofollow noopener'> Ready Player One</a> will find themselves transported into a world of geeky allusions, a diverse cast of characters, and honestly, a really, really good time.<br/><br/>Now it's inevitable to compare <i>Armada</i> to <i>RPO</i> because of Cline centering both around</span>
  <span id="freeText4517813423222992812" style="display:none"><i>"I was staring out the classroom window and daydreaming of adventure when I spotted the flying saucer."</i><br /><br />From the very first sentence of the book, Ernest Cline takes the reader on a heart-pounding, laser-shooting, smile-inducing adventure. Fans of his first novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One" title="Ready Player One by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener"> Ready Player One</a> will find themselves transported into a world of geeky allusions, a diverse cast of characters, and honestly, a really, really good time.<br /><br />Now it's inevitable to compare <i>Armada</i> to <i>RPO</i> because of Cline centering both around the idea of video games and virtual reality. However, while there are similarities (the narrator Zack is quite similar in voice to <i>RPO</i>'s Wade Watts; tons of nerdy references, action-adventure, and more), this one still stands apart and on its own. <br /><br />I seriously couldn't put this book down. It started off a bit slow, very technical as far as video game and science fiction terminology goes, and took a bit to get into the action. But once it did, I ate this book up. The pacing was <b>so quick</b> that I felt compelled to read on. Most of the action of the book takes place in 24 hours. It's insane. And Zack is a snarky, likeable, albeit a bit average, narrator that I enjoyed getting inside his head. And of course there are a few plot twists thrown in that shocked me. <br /><br />One of my favorite aspects of the book was the sort of alternate history/conspiracy theories that are presented to you. Also a female U.S. president; yes please. <br /><br />But of course, I had a few minor issues with how Cline represented the love interest (talk about manic pixie dream girl), and the ending was just as fast-paced as the rest of the book. I would've been totally fine with 50 more pages to flesh out that resolution. Or at least give me a sequel! It was just so much to take in all at once--for us and for Zack--that I wanted more time and more information. <br /><br />Overall I was pleased with this one. I had pretty high expectations, which might be unfair to the author, but <i>RPO</i> was just so darn great that how could I not?! And while I wouldn't say I was 100% satisfied, it was still a fun, exciting, solid reading experience that I hope others are pleased with too. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4517813423222992812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9324602335420663286">I gave this book 2 stars.<br/><br/>I am going to preface my review by saying I really didn't enjoy reading this book very much. I will admit that it had a lot of hype and big shoes to fill, coming after Ready Player One, but for me it completely fell flat.<br/><br/>Maybe someone really really into flight sim and tactical war games will appreciate this book more, but I found it very dull.   <span id="freeText9324602335420663286" style="display:none">I gave this book 2 stars.<br /><br />I am going to preface my review by saying I really didn't enjoy reading this book very much. I will admit that it had a lot of hype and big shoes to fill, coming after Ready Player One, but for me it completely fell flat.<br /><br />Maybe someone really really into flight sim and tactical war games will appreciate this book more, but I found it very dull. So much of the story involved having things explained to me and there was very little immediate action, which was hard to get into at best - a snorefest at worst.<br /><br />Not only did the main character experience insta-love, but it seemed literally everyone else in the book did too. Who even WAS Lex? <br /><br />The pop culture references were SO forced, and often carried the pattern of "...like that one guy in that one scene of that one movie!" Uninspired. Irritating. Repetitive.<br />I found the plot predictable, INCREDIBLY unbelievable, and so, so many things felt too easy, too convenient. I just don't buy any of it. I don't want to spoil the plot, but I just couldn't get myself to believe any of it was plausible. And that ending! Not exciting! So meh!<br /><br />Overall, I just didn't enjoy it very much. I think the idea was there, but it just didn't work for me.</span>

<div id="review_833488569" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/833488569" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10673439-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405037359p2/10673439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/833488569?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/10673439-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10673439-amanda?shelf=2015">2015</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer833488569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2864269080746228433">My final thoughts below.<br/><br/>The only thing I liked about this was the mix tape playlist at the end.<br/><br/>There was nothing original or innovative about this story. I tried to look at it from a, "what if this happened to me in real like kind of thing and how cool that would be", but it wasn't. It felt like a rehashing of something that has been done countless times, and done better I might add. And even though Ernest Cline references those exact things, Wargames, Enders Game, The Last Starfigher, Starwars </span>
  <span id="freeText2864269080746228433" style="display:none">My final thoughts below.<br /><br />The only thing I liked about this was the mix tape playlist at the end.<br /><br />There was nothing original or innovative about this story. I tried to look at it from a, "what if this happened to me in real like kind of thing and how cool that would be", but it wasn't. It felt like a rehashing of something that has been done countless times, and done better I might add. And even though Ernest Cline references those exact things, Wargames, Enders Game, The Last Starfigher, Starwars etc, he's not doing a variation of it, just flat out doing the same thing. THE SAME EXACT PLOT.<br /><br />On top of that, a kid his age would not reference the 80's films with his friends. The main character has a nostalgic connection to old games and movies because of his dad, so I'll buy that, but all of his friends too? It just didn't seem realistic. I haven't even seen all those movies. That media would be way too old for a kid his age since he's born in the later 2000's. <br /><br />Also the amount of pop culture references was tiring. Leeroy Jenkins was a really funny relevant thing 10 years ago, that would NOT be mentioned in what ever fictional game he was playing. It just wouldn't make any sense to bring it up unless you were playing World of Warcraft. (Leeroy Jenkins is a World of Warcraft reference.) Unless it made a come back on the internet, they wouldn't be saying it. On top of everything he says had to be a reference to something that is really in your face and he's just pulling on the nostalgia card. You like hearing about Obi-wan because you like Starwars. That doesn't make this a good book though.<br /><br />Maybe I went into this too seriously and maybe this book is making fun of itself, but I didn't feel like it came off that way. The twists and cliche's were just too much and the entire story was just so painfully predictable. It didn't do anything to show me that it was a parody of the many classics mentioned or doing anything different. <br /><br />I'd rather just read Ender's Game again.</span>

<div id="review_1297203596" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1297203596" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1297203596?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=o-captain-my-captain">o-captain-my-captain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297203596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16568582047521381281"><b>Sale Alert 23May17 on Amazon for $2.99 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Armada-novel-author-Ready-Player-ebook/dp/B00TNDID0O/ref=br_prlt_grdDy_pdt-8?_encoding=UTF8&pd_rd_r=NJRBZYWWYEGQBHJR5DP2&pd_rd_w=VDxCa&pd_rd_wg=uRanS&pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-3&pf_rd_r=NJRBZYWWYEGQBHJR5DP2&pf_rd_r=NJRBZYWWYEGQBHJR5DP2&pf_rd_t=101&pf_rd_p=15f652e8-a362-454e-89e2-ac3b15b28c11&pf_rd_p=15f652e8-a362-454e-89e2-ac3b15b28c11&pf_rd_i=7533915011' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here</a></b><br/><br/>Before you pick this book up you need to ask yourself…<b>’Am I ready to get my geek on???’</b> As soon as I saw that Ernest Cline author of Ready Player One had another book coming out and it was narrated by Wil Wheaton my amazon/audible one click pre-order went cRaZy and I shoved my money at them.<br/><br/>I’m just going to put it out there <b>I liked Ready Player One more</b>. So if you haven’t ready that yet GO GET IT!!! But Armada has some very nice characteristics too tha</span>
  <span id="freeText16568582047521381281" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert 23May17 on Amazon for $2.99 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Armada-novel-author-Ready-Player-ebook/dp/B00TNDID0O/ref=br_prlt_grdDy_pdt-8?_encoding=UTF8&amp;pd_rd_r=NJRBZYWWYEGQBHJR5DP2&amp;pd_rd_w=VDxCa&amp;pd_rd_wg=uRanS&amp;pf_rd_m=ATVPDKIKX0DER&amp;pf_rd_s=merchandised-search-3&amp;pf_rd_r=NJRBZYWWYEGQBHJR5DP2&amp;pf_rd_r=NJRBZYWWYEGQBHJR5DP2&amp;pf_rd_t=101&amp;pf_rd_p=15f652e8-a362-454e-89e2-ac3b15b28c11&amp;pf_rd_p=15f652e8-a362-454e-89e2-ac3b15b28c11&amp;pf_rd_i=7533915011" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a></b><br /><br />Before you pick this book up you need to ask yourself…<b>’Am I ready to get my geek on???’</b> As soon as I saw that Ernest Cline author of Ready Player One had another book coming out and it was narrated by Wil Wheaton my amazon/audible one click pre-order went cRaZy and I shoved my money at them.<br /><br />I’m just going to put it out there <b>I liked Ready Player One more</b>. So if you haven’t ready that yet GO GET IT!!! But Armada has some very nice characteristics too that should make it a Pop Culture/Sci-Fi/Fantasy/Gamer lover’s dream. I know that my geek meter was pegged out as I had the best time looking to catch movie lines, character references and gaming lingo and there was a plethora of that dropped all throughout the story. <br /><br />The entire premise of the book really boils down to this –<br /><blockquote>
  <i> What if they’re using videogames to train us to fight without us even knowing it? Like Mr. Miyagi in The Karate Kid, when he made Daniel-san paint his house, sand his deck, and wax all of his cars—he was training him and he didn’t even realize it! Wax on, wax off—but on a global scale!</i>
</blockquote><br />So pretty much think of a mash up of things like The Last Star Fighter and Ender’s Game (which are referenced many times in the story along with Star Wars and Star Trek). Hey even though I’ve seen this plot before it is a good premise and a lot of fun for the story.<br /><br />Zack is a kid with daddy issues and possibly a moderate gaming addiction. He is trying to decide whether his fantasy life has become reality or if he is just hallucinating when he sees an alien spacecraft from his favorite MMORPG (Massive Multiplayer Online Role Playing Game) Armada outside his school. Maybe he is going crazy or maybe…just maybe all the Sci-Fi movies, TV Shows and Books since the 70s has all been preparing us for THIS exact moment in time. That is when everything goes wonky and gets crazy.<br /><br />There are some fantastically funny side characters that give us plenty of opportunity for some geeked out fun of dropping movie quotes, song lyrics and debates on the best cinema Melee Weapon.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Sting wasn’t even really a sword,” Diehl was saying. “It was more like a glow-in-the-dark Hobbit butter knife, used to spread jam on scones and lembas bread and shit.”<br />Cruz rolled his eyes. “’Your love of the halflings’ leaf has clearly slowed your mind,’” he quoted. “Sting was an Elvish blade, forged in Gondolin in the First Age! It could cut through almost anything! And its blade only glowed when it detected the presence of orcs or goblins nearby. What does Mjolnir detect? Fake accents and frosted hair?”</i>
</blockquote><br />And possibly my favorite since I also like to use swear words from worlds in books and movies…<i>Airsick Lowlanders!!!</i> &lt;--- this is my own personal favorite to use. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Shit!” I heard Diehl shout over the comm. “I just lost my gorram shields because I’m already out of frakkin’ power!” <br />“Dude,” Cruz said. “You shouldn’t mix swears from different universes.” <br />“Says who?” Diehl shot back. “Besides, what if BSG and Firefly took place in the same universe? You ever consider that?”</i>
</blockquote><br />Remarkably I’ve had discussions similar to this with Hubs and friends so this book easily called to me. There were shout outs to Authors like Patrick Rothfuss and Orsen Scott Card, along with so many Star Trek and Star Wars references I couldn’t keep track. Also Cline hit on Galaxy Quest, Navigator, Aliens, 2001 a Space Odyssey, Iron Eagle, Top Gun…Say Anything (okay you might not think that one fits but it totally does) and much much more. There is even just enough time for a minor blooming romance to start. So you might be asking yourself…<b>Why Robin did you only give it 3 stars? </b> Well as much as I loved the pop culture geek fest in this I got bored with the action scenes and I’m iffy on how I feel about the ending.<br /><br />My gaming experience is limited to World of Warcraft, Bejeweled, Wii, Super Mario Cart and Candy Crush…don’t judge me. I’m not a huge fan of first person shooter games and a large portion of the fighting is based on that. My imagination totally sucks when it comes to flying robots and ship fighting one another in space shooting lasers. I KNOW it should be exciting and if someone had pulled out a Katana and started hacking away through enemy lines I would have totally dug it and been able to really imagine it well, but I struggled so much with this part of the story and lost a little interest in it.<br /><br />Also Ready Player One had an upbeat ending and a HEA feeling to it. While this is not all destruction and mayhem, although there was a lot of that, the ending didn’t leave me feeling happy or even sad I was just OH…I’m not sure I liked that. I’m not sure I didn’t like it either but definitely felt odd about it. I was slightly upset that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[seriously HUGE end of book spoiler<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>OKAY YOU WERE WARNED</b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Zack gets his dad back to fight with to save the world for like A DAY, in which time they make up and come to an understanding, cuz end of the world and all and there is a heartfelt reunion with his mother and father and then….HE SACRIFICES HISSELF and dies. *sigh* I didn’t like that part at all. Then the epilogue a year later, his mom who lost her husband all over again has a baby from the one day reunion and they are visiting his grave again….I really actually hated this part. Sure he saved the world but it just didn’t seem necessary to kill him off…again. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />While the ending does close out this book to be read as a stand-alone, there is just enough of an opening for there to be a sequel down the line. <b> Would I read it???</b> WELL YESSS of coarse I would and I’d probably autobuy it as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16568582047521381281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
